# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Grafana Legacy Alerting to Unified Alerting Migration

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in grafana/grafana that implement both the legacy alerting engine and the unified alerting (ngalert) engine: the legacy alert rule storage, the unified alert rule storage, and the migration script that converts legacy rules to unified format.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the migration domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec` (grafana/grafana)
- `sg-evals/grafana-loki` (grafana/loki)
- `sg-evals/grafana-mimir` (grafana/mimir)

## Summary

I found and documented the Go source files implementing Grafana's legacy alerting to unified alerting migration:

### Key Findings:

**35 Core Files** including:
- **Legacy Alerting**: `pkg/services/sqlstore/migrations/alert_mig.go`
- **Unified Alerting (ngalert)**: Core engine in `pkg/services/ngalert/`
- **Migration Scripts**: Complete migration orchestration in `pkg/services/sqlstore/migrations/ualert/`
- **Legacy Storage Bridges**: Compatibility layers for gradual migration

### Main Components:

1. **Migration System** (`pkg/services/sqlstore/migrations/ualert/`):
   - `ualert.go` - Core migration handler
   - `tables.go` - Schema definitions for alert_rule, alert_configuration, alert_instance tables
   - Multiple migration files for org state, created folders, and access control

2. **Unified Alerting Engine** (`pkg/services/ngalert/`):
   - AlertRule model with UID, OrgID, RuleGroup, NoDataState, ExecErrState
   - DBstore for persistence
   - AlertNG main service
   - Provisioning system for rule management

3. **Legacy Storage Bridges**: Compatibility layer supporting format conversion and backward compatibility with legacy alertmanager configurations

4. **Provisioning**: Alert rule configuration management from files and APIs

The answer file contains detailed narrative explanation, symbol definitions, and call chains showing how the migration system works to convert legacy alert rules to the unified alerting format.

`AddTablesMigrations()`: Creates alert_rule, alert_rule_version, alert_instance, alert_configuration tables\\n   - `addAlertRuleMigrations()`: Creates the alert_rule table with columns for org_id, title, condition, data, interval_seconds, namespace_uid, rule_group\\n   - `addAlertmanagerConfigMigrations()`: Creates alert_configuration table for storing alertmanager configurations\\n   - Includes index creation and column modifications for schema evolution\\n\\n3. **org_upgrade_state_mig.go**: Tracks alerting type per organization (Legacy vs UnifiedAlerting)\\n\\n4. **created_folders_mig.go**: Migrates records of folders created during the legacy alert migration process\\n\\n5. **migration_service_migration.go**: Moves legacy alert migration status from migration log to kvstore with namespace \\\"ngalert.migration\\\"\\n\\n6. **accesscontrol/alerting.go**: Migrates alerting-related permissions and action names\\n\\n## Legacy Storage Bridges\\nMultiple legacy storage implementations provide compatibility between old and new systems:\\n\\n1. **Alertmanager Configuration**: `pkg/services/ngalert/notifier/legacy_storage/config.go` implements `alertmanagerConfigStoreImpl` for reading/writing legacy Alertmanager configurations\\n\\n2. **Receiver Management**: `pkg/services/ngalert/notifier/legacy_storage/` contains:\\n   -
